## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves determining the rate law for a chemical reaction. The rate of change of concentration dA/dt typically depends on the concentration A through power-law or other nonlinear relationships, and the presence of time t as a variable suggests possible time-dependent rate coefficients, external forcing, or autocatalytic/complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to concentration squared)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- First-order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (reversible first-order reaction approaching equilibrium)
- Second-order reversible: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (quadratic rate law from reversible bimolecular reaction)
- Autocatalytic rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate coefficient: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changing exponentially with time)
- Linear time-modulated rate: dA_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * A (linearly varying rate coefficient)
- Fractional-order with time: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (power-law dependence on both A and t)
- Oscillatory forcing: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (periodic external perturbation)
- Competitive inhibition analog: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (saturation in rate at high concentration)
- Cubic rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 + c1 * A (third-order with first-order terms)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order kinetics, surface-mediated reactions)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration dependence (no t) → classical rate law dA/dt = k*A^n; check if t is irrelevant
- Negative dA/dt values → consumption/decay reaction; positive values → production or autocatalysis
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) → autocatalytic or equilibrium-approaching behavior with fixed total concentration
- Explicit time dependence in rate → photochemical reactions, temperature ramps, or catalyst deactivation
- Rate approaching zero as A→0 → power-law with positive exponent; rate finite at A=0 → zero-order or external source term
- Polynomial in A with alternating signs → reversible reactions with forward and backward steps
- Rational functions of A → enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed mechanisms with saturation
- Product of power laws in t and A → diffusion-limited kinetics or fractal reaction kinetics

This is: `A * [c_log * log(c_inner * t + 1) + c_exp * exp(-c_decay * t)]`

where the two main components are:

2. A decaying exponential term: `A * (-0.9112) * exp(-0.08901*t)`

**Key observations about GT:**
- Two terms, both multiplied by A
- One is `exp(negative * t)` (decaying exponential)
- One is `log(linear_in_t + 1)`

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(c*t) + 1)` terms (candidates 11, 12, 17, 21, 24, 25, 27):**

For `log(c6*exp(c7*t) + 1)`: When `c7 → 0`, `log(c6*exp(0) + 1) = log(c6+1)` = constant. This doesn't give `log(c*t+1)`.

Actually, let me reconsider. Can `log(c*exp(d*t) + 1)` approximate `log(a*t + 1)`? Not exactly for all t.

**Candidates with `cos(c*log(c*t+1))` or `sin(c*log(c*t+1)+c)` terms:**

If I set the frequency parameter to 0: `cos(0*log(...)) = cos(0) = 1` → constant.
`sin(0*log(...) + c4) = sin(c4)` → constant.

But `sin(c2*log(c3*t+1) + c4)`: if I set `c2 = 1` and `c4 = π/2`, then `sin(log(c3*t+1) + π/2) = cos(log(c3*t+1))`. Not what I need.

Hmm, none of these directly give `log(c*t+1)`.

**Candidate 21:** `A*c0*log(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1) + A*c3*t + A*c4*exp(c5*t) + A*c6*t*exp(c5*t) + A*c7*t*log(c8*t + 1)`

This has `A*c7*t*log(c8*t + 1)` — not quite `log(c*t+1)`.
And `A*c0*log(c1*exp(c2*t) + 1)`: if `c1` is very small and `c2` is very small... Let me think. When `c1*exp(c2*t) << 1`, `log(1 + x) ≈ x`, so this becomes `c0*c1*exp(c2*t)`. That's just another exponential.

Actually wait - if `c2 = 0`: `log(c1 + 1)` = constant. Not helpful.

**None of the candidates contain a plain `log(c*t + c)` term.** The GT requires a `log(linear in t)` term, but the candidates only have log composed with exponentials, or log inside trig functions, or `t*log(...)`.

Since no candidate has a bare `log(c*t + 1)` term (they all have log inside sin/cos, or log of exponentials, or t*log), none can exactly reproduce the GT's logarithmic term.

- `log(c*exp(c*t) + 1)`
- `t*log(c*t + 1)`

None of these can produce a bare `log(c*t + 1)` for arbitrary t.
